The folk-rnn (v2) Session Book
Volume 5 of 10⇤

This work is licensed under a Creative Commons Attribution 4.0 International License.

⇤ Thank you to Bob L. Sturm, João Felipe Santos, Oded Ben-Tal, Iryna Korshunova, and the many contributors
of thesession.org.

1

Forward
The approximately 3,000 tune transcriptions in this volume have been generated entirely by a
computerised system named folk-rnn (v2). We trained this system on over 23,000 tunes transcribed
and contributed by users of thesession.org in ABC notation (abcnotation.com). Many of these
tunes are traditional to Ireland and the UK. The folk-rnn (v2) system is essentially a statistical
model that can predict sequences of tokens that resemble ABC notation. This system once trained
can generate an endless number of new tune transcriptions. So, over a few days in September 2016,
we had it generate 30,000 of them.
The volumes in this collection archive this burst of “creative” computation of the folk-rnn (v2)
system. Each tune here appears as ABC and in sta↵ notation. We have not corrected or improved
any of the transcriptions in these volumes, but we have adapted and performed some of them, e.g.,
#488, #2857, and #4542. We have also synthesised many transcriptions to create “The Endless
folk-rnn Traditional Music Session”: www.eecs.qmul.ac.uk/⇠sturm/research/RNNIrishTrad/.
We have so far developed two other versions of the folk-rnn system. The first, v1, was a basic
model that predicts characters in one large file. The second, v2, uses a revised representation of the
transcriptions, and predicts tokens in individual transcriptions. The third version, v3, encompasses
yet another revision of the representation. We have also applied v1 and v3 to generating more
volumes of computer-generated tune transcriptions — totalling about 100,000 transcriptions now.
All volumes can be found at the project website: github.com/IraKorshunova/folk-rnn.
Why have we done this? We have not done this because we think the world needs 100,000 new
but mediocre tunes. We have not done this because we believe the rich tradition of music from
Ireland in the UK is so simple that “even a computer can do it.” We have done this because we
believe artificial intelligence can provide human creators and music practitioners with useful tools.
In fact, we want to encourage anyone anywhere to use the material in this volume in any way, and
so we are licensing all transcriptions in this volume under a “Creative Commons Attribution 4.0
International License”.
Several examples of how these transcriptions have been used to create new music can be found
at the project website: github.com/IraKorshunova/folk-rnn. Our system is also completely open
and free to use. All we ask in return is to be made aware when such use has occurred. In such
instance, please send an e-mail to the project leader, Bob L. Sturm (b.sturm@qmul.ac.uk).
Bob L. Sturm, Dec. 31 2017 in London
